  44. This product does exactly what it says that it will, however, you need to make sure that you know a few things about it before purchasing it and using it.<br /><br />1. It comes with a European plug and it will need an adapter if you are using it in the US. I was fairly upset when I opened the box being here in America and having to run to the store to buy an adapter before being able to try it out. If you're in America add an adapter to your cart before you check out and save yourself the hassle. If you're in Europe then your plugs look weird lol<br /><br />2. Make sure that you really press the bulbs into place. It took a little more force than I would have thought but the bulbs didn't break and they made a snapping sound when properly installed.<br /><br />3. There is a tray at the bottom of the lamp that slides in and out. It is coated with a sheet of blue plastic protectant that must be pulled off PRIOR to use. If you don't pull it off then the UV rays won't be able to bounce around the product and you may not get the drying effect you need.<br /><br />4. YOU WILL HAVE TO CLEAN YOUR NAILS WITH A COTTON BALL DIPPED IN ALCOHOL. Yes, they will be sticky when they come out even if you process them repeatedly. This isn't because the lamp isn't working; you just have to clean them afterward.<br /><br />I cured my daughter's nails tonight with Gelish Top It Off over regular polish and it cured them great. Again, after research, I attributed this to curing times. So manicure number 3 took me two hours! No joke! I cured at least 3 times longer than instructions and since you can only do one hand at a time in this thing, it took forever. I still had polish that I could kind of \\"dent\\" with my finger nail and again, chipping within 3 days and dull finish.<br /><br />After even MORE research, I am convinced that I will never get salon results with this light. Plus, I offered to do my family and friends' nails when I got all the stuff (polish, light, etc) and there is no way I'm going to do that with these cure times! I'm cutting my losses and buying the Royal for $50. Sigh.<br /><br />NOTE: Be very careful with the light bulbs in this light. They fall out easily and you have to be very careful to get them in without jamming and breaking things.

  363. I bought this more than a year ago and at first I hated this and just put it away instead of sending it back. Later I got it out and tried again to no avail. Like all the one-star reviewers, I thought it wasn't curing. As some of the reviewers, who love this product, have said, \\"The bad reviewers don't know how to use it.\\" THEY WERE RIGHT!! It really pays to read these reviews when you get a product that even the makers don't know how to use as indicated in their lack of useful directions.<br /><br />So I was looking for another UV light, higher wattage because I thought it would work better. In reading over the reviews and watching a few YouTube videos I found 3 very helpful things.<br /><br />1) After curing, there WILL be stickiness that must be removed with alcohol on a cotton cloth (lint free). Who knows to do this when they don't do it at the salon?!<br /><br />2) I was reading a review for another product that said you are supposed to remove all the blue film from the mirrors. I'm pretty sure the instructions for Salon Edge didn't say to remove the blue film from the bottom (and not really sure you should) but I can't be sure because I cannot locate my directions and could not find it online. You tube videos show the film still there. In any case, I DID remove it which was very easy.<br /><br />3) You should cure after each coat of polish: base, color, another layer of color, top coat. I was not doing this before.<br /><br />So I did my nails again armed with helpful hints and after removing the blue film on the bottom. There was still that stickiness but seemingly not near as much as before. I am not sure if it is from removing the blue film, curing after each layer of polish, or both. Either way, I just wiped off the stickiness with the alcohol and cotton cloth (cut up old t-shirt) and VOILA! I went about my day with no problem.<br /><br />This is a nice inexpensive UV light that works well. Oh and BTW I'm still using my original light bulbs after over a year but then I have only used this 3 times. I think when I have to replace the bulbs I might just get an LED lamp since you don't have to replace the bulbs near as often.

  525. For those who live outside of US and wish to buy this lamp (actually as well as any other appliance designed and made in the US), please carefully read below note:<br /><br />Note: Since the lamps are designed and made in the US. The power voltage used by these lamps is 110V. If you are purchasing the lamp from a different country e.g. Australia, you are required to use a step down transformer which will reduce the power supply to the lamp from 220-240V to 110V. Different countries have a different Voltage and if the country you are in has a power voltage of more than 110V, you will need to use a step down transformer to connect the lamp. Connecting the lamp directly to the power supply will result in a power surge burning the wiring and the lamp. This is something which cannot be rectified neither can the product be exchanged.<br /><br />I forgot about power voltage and burnt mine.......<br />And here I would like to note that there is no sign or note neither on the lamp itself nor on its package about its voltage, which I believe is not correct...

  733. Easy to use and has saved me LOTS of $$ doing my own manicures at home!!!<br /><br />My process is as follows:<br />1) Clean my natural nails of all previous gel*, push back cuticles, then buff to smooth the nail.<br />2) Apply one coat of Shellac base, cure with lamp for 120 secs.<br />3) Apply one thin coat of colored Gel (I use Gellish, Shellac and OPI), cure with lamp for 120 secs.<br />4) Apply a second thin coat of colored Gel, cure with lamp for 120 secs.<br />5) OPTIONAL - Apply a thin coat of sparkly Gel if desired (personally I LOVE sparkles!!), cure with lamp for 120 secs.<br />6) Apply the final coat of Shallac top, then cure with lamp for TWO ROUNDS of 120 secs.<br /><br />When I'm done I have a gorgeous manicure that lasts at least 2 weeks. At that point, I'll usually change the color out because the growth from the cuticle is so obvious, but not because the gel has chipped or lifted. I've successfully done my own pedicures too and those last at least a month before the growth shows (still no chipping).<br /><br />The entire process from start to finish takes about 20-30 mins if starting with clean nails, 45-60 mins if I'm removing old gel; but most of that is getting the nails ready to put the gel on. If I'm doing my own I'll catch up on my DVR while doing my nails (multitasking ;-p) or if I'm doing my friend's or my mom's it's great time to just catch up on stuff. &lt;3 It's turned into a great way not only to save money on my own mani/pedis, but also on gift giving... my friends LOVE free manicures.<br /><br />* One thing that I have learned for the health of your natural nail, is that soaking with acetone to loosen the gel up is WAY, WAY better than just peeling the gel off. Just soak a cotton ball with acetone, place over the old gel, cover the finger tip with foil and wait 15 minutes. Scrape off what you can and if there's any left, allow to soak again in 5 min intervals, until it's all gone.

  776. After researching 10+ machines, and countless articles on gel manicures, I decided to give this one a try.<br /><br />Now, I've had it for all of 45 minutes. My two first major complaints are within seconds of opening the box. It's not white. It's a light pink/liliac colored machine. It's not even close to white. Second, there are absolutely zero directions in the box. So, I had to fend for myself and wing it as far as putting the bulbs in. Previous reviews helped, you really need to put force for the bulbs to lock in place. The blue bottom tray slides out completely and detaches so you can get the bulbs in easier. My machine must have been previously returned because it has little dings, dents, scratches and scuffs. That's pretty much it for the cons. I'm not sure why so many people received ones where the plug doesn't work USA style, mine looked and worked fine.<br /><br />I decided to still give it a try before I made up my mind to return and consider reordering the same item. I just got a regular acrylic manicure earlier today, with Essie nail polish. I read online you could just use regular polish and put a gel coat on top to cure and be done, so I did just that. HOWEVER, regular polish needs a few hours to dry out completely to bond to your nail, unlike gel manicures that are dried out immediately(hence no need to sit and dry). Most websites said 24 hours. I waited ~7 hours. All I did was apply a thin top coat to one hand, set in the machine for the 120 seconds(timer is a great feature) and then the other hand, then I repeated. ***IMPORTANT*** most people that get gel manicures don't realize right before they send you on your way they take a cotton ball or clothe and put alcohol on it and wipe the excess top gel coat off your nails. Most people just think they're wiping lotion off or oil to make the nails shine but it's actually alcohol. (hard to believe because alcohol takes off regular nail polish) So, most of the 1 reviews on here are that the nails are &#34;sticky&#34; after. That's how they are in the salon too. I used 70% rubbing alcohol (most sites say to use 99% but this worked perfectly fine for me, and I would recommend 70% because using a higher strength may eat through and wipe a fresh manicure off too) and you just have to wipe off the excess gel. I feel like this is a HUGE part in why people return the machine. The nails aren't supposed to dry out completely, you can actually see the curing process if you look into the machine at your hand(I don't recommend- its pretty bright!) You can see the change of color in the light, but the polish remains the same color outside of the machine- this was a good indicator to me that the polish was curing because I remember seeing it when I'd stick my hands in the machine at the salon and only the ones with the top gel coat looked a crazy color in the machine but normal when I took them out) On a side note, I can tell how much stronger/thicker my nails feel using the gel top coat over my manicure(I have very brittle nails so this is super exciting!)<br /><br />Other than the fact mine looked used, no directions, and weird tint of pink to my machine- it does the job fine. I'd otherwise so far give it a 5 star rating. I'm excited to use it with actual gel polish. I use &#34;LeChat Perfect Match High Gloss Top Gel Sealer&#34;. I also have their ultra-think base varnish(got both for $23 on ebay). I've always gotten gel manicures with their products at salons. I'd highly recommend to try their brand. They also sell them in Dou's- the gel polish and regular acrylic polish sets for about $12 on ebay, so you can use regular polish on toes if you don't feel like going through the gel- curing process. I also bought their primer bond(LeChat Nobility Primer Bond-ebay $6.50) which is what most salons put on your nails before the base coat.<br /><br />As far as doing actual gel manicures, you have to replicate how salons do it- I recommend to use the primer bond, then do a base coaton one hand, cure for 120 seconds, do the same to the other hand, then I did two nails on one hand, cured, then did two nails on the other hand and cured and repeated til I got through a second coat on each nail. I'm not sure the chemistry behind it but thats how my nail salon does it, and it worked well for me at salons so I would assume the same for at home. my only concern is the amount of UV light penetrating my hands(I worried about this at salons too but the salon i've been at for the last year uses UV protection gloves- another wise investment!) Then you top the manicure off with gel top coat, two nails at a time and cure between. It does take a lot longer as opposed to someone else doing your nails so you can constantly just switch out hands but it seems to give the exact same result. Again, you need to wipe the excess gel top coat off.<br /><br />I'll revamp my review when I get my gel polish in the mail and try again- I'll actually experiment since I bought the duo set and do one hand regular polish with a bottom and top gel coat and the other in gel polish since they're the same color/brand and update how long they last/hold up :)
